  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f30b25cb-4775-45c9-bd12-39dd19ebc96f'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer10125024038657595723">Imaginez une Terre poncée, avec en son centre une bande de cinq mille kilomètres de large et sur ses franges un miroir de glace à peine rayable, inhabité.   <span id="freeText10125024038657595723" style="display:none">Imaginez une Terre poncée, avec en son centre une bande de cinq mille kilomètres de large et sur ses franges un miroir de glace à peine rayable, inhabité. Imaginez qu’un vent féroce en rince la surface. Que les villages qui s’y sont accrochés, avec leurs maisons en goutte d’eau, les chars à voile qui la strient, les airpailleurs debout en plein flot, tous résistent. Imaginez qu’en Extrême-Aval ait été formé un bloc d’élite d’une vingtaine d’enfants aptes à remonter au cran, rafale en gueule, leur vie durant, le vent jusqu’à sa source, à ce jour jamais atteinte : l’Extrême-Amont.<br />Mon nom est Sov Strochnis, scribe. Mon nom est Caracole le troubadour et Oroshi Melicerte, aéromaître. Je m’appelle aussi Golgoth, traceur de la Horde, Arval l’éclaireur et parfois même Larco lorsque je braconne l’azur à la cage volante. Ensemble, nous formons la Horde du Contrevent. Il en a existé trente-trois en huit siècles, toutes infructueuses. Je vous parle au nom de la trente-quatrième : sans doute l’ultime.</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_45434164" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/45434164" />
    <a title="Roxane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1148105-roxane"><img alt="Roxane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1519370095p2/1148105.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/45434164?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Roxane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Roxane" href="/user/show/1148105-roxane">Roxane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1148105-roxane?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1148105-roxane?shelf=french">french</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer45434164" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9222147521363867054">This little (just above 700 pages long!) jewel won the Grand Prix de l'Imaginaire back in 2006. It's the most prestigious French award as far as speculative fiction is concerned. Previous winners include Pierre Bordage, Jean-Pierre Andrevon, Fabrice Colin, Maurice G. Dantec and Francis Berthelot in the French fiction category and Robert Charles Wilson, Ursula K. Le Guin, Graham Joyce, Christopher Priest and Jeffrey Ford in the foreign fiction category.<br/><br/>Alain Damasio is probably one of France's mo</span>
  <span id="freeText9222147521363867054" style="display:none">This little (just above 700 pages long!) jewel won the Grand Prix de l'Imaginaire back in 2006. It's the most prestigious French award as far as speculative fiction is concerned. Previous winners include Pierre Bordage, Jean-Pierre Andrevon, Fabrice Colin, Maurice G. Dantec and Francis Berthelot in the French fiction category and Robert Charles Wilson, Ursula K. Le Guin, Graham Joyce, Christopher Priest and Jeffrey Ford in the foreign fiction category.<br /><br />Alain Damasio is probably one of France's most promising young voices and La Horde du Contrevent is just his second novel. He is most acknowledged in science fiction circles and that's just too bad for mainstream readers, writers and publishers who just don't know what they are missing out on. Still, the most amazing thing is that Damasio hardly reads any science fiction or fantasy at all. What he does read however is a lot of philosophy and that says a lot about science fiction writers being modern day philosophers. But that's a whole other debate, isn't it?<br /><br />Let me tell you one thing though, whether you are a speculative fiction reader or not, you've *never* read anything like this book. And I do mean NEVER. More than just treating the book as a simple medium to deliver a message, Damasio has conceived this specific work as a book universe. The medium is intimately linked to the message and well, I'm sad to say it, but this remarkable achievement simply makes the book intranslatable. You'd have to rewrite entire parts of the book to make them work in another language. It'd be a tremendous work and you'd never be sure whether or not you'd be betraying the author's original speech.<br /><br />You know something about this book is different as soon as you pick it up and start browsing through its content: the pages start at 700 and decrease all the way down to 0. A limited edition of the book was released with a soundtrack. Unfortunately, I wasn't able to put my hands on it, but the very concept of a book having its own soundtrack is one that I find extremely relevant and original. I read with music and I often associate discs or tracks with specific books or even chapters. Sometimes it happens by accident. For example, it is just happens to be a new CD that I'm listening to while reading a book, but, at others times, the choices can be more deliberate. Anyway, I don't know of any other instances when a publisher has released a book with a soundtrack, so the idea is original enough to be toyed with. I know Mélanie Fazi, another talented young French author and translator, has released on her blog the name of the tracks she was listening to while writing a given piece of fiction but it's nothing quite as elaborate as actually putting together a book soundtrack.<br /><br />But there's so much more about this book and it's just about time I got around to telling you about the plot, isn't it?<br /><br />In a devastated world, living to the rhythms of the unbearable winds which rule it, an organization selects, raises and trains children from a very young age so that they will become the next horde. The 34th horde counts 23 members; each has a specific function (tracer, scribe, troubadour, hunter, protector, carer, maker of fire, wood maker, etc.). They have been traveling the world for over 30 years in search of the origin of the wind.<br /><br />Damasio has created a world in which the wind is omnipresent and its divine character is alluded to several times throughout the book. The narration is not told from a single point of view, each one of the 23 characters gets a go! To succeed in pulling this off without confusing his reader says a lot about the author's talent. Furthermore, each switch of point of view is announced by a sign belonging to a character. So not only do you have to deal with 23 characters but you also have to remember each character's personal symbol... I did it effortlessly and this has nothing to do with any unparalleled memorization capacity of mine because, well, let's face it, what I usually have an unparalleled capacity for is forgetting things. The polyphonic dimension of the book might be what initially puts you off, but trust me, you'll get the hang of it faster than you think and in the end, the polyphony is precisely the book's greatest quality.<br /><br />23 characters which have been living with one another for over 30 years, who know nothing else besides fighting the wind, going forward no matter what, who don't always get along, who love, hate and don't understand one another, let alone the purpose or utility of their mission which really is a religious one. Damasio weaves a wonderful, touching and suspenseful story about faith, friendship, hardships and science. The mythology and technology he creates around the wind and the way the inhabitants try and often fail to adapt to its raging strength is truly unparalleled.<br /><br />I very strongly recommend this book to anyone who reads French. This book is a very singular experience all together and it renewed my passion for reading (not that it has gone anywhere, but it's like a habit which requires things to be spiced up once in a while and this book did the trick).</span>
  <a data-text-id="9222147521363867054" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_129918838" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/129918838" />
    <a title="Ed Erwin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1411444-ed-erwin"><img alt="Ed Erwin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604431321p2/1411444.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/129918838?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ed Erwin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ed Erwin" href="/user/show/1411444-ed-erwin">Ed Erwin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1411444-ed-erwin?shelf=sf-francaise">sf-francaise</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer129918838" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3660976205389201754">I made it to the end! I can hardly believe it! <br/><br/>This was a very difficult book to get through. 700 pages of dense, unusual text full of stylistic invention and word-play, with constantly changing narrators, set in a world unlike any I've ever encountered. And in, what is for me, a foreign language.<br/><br/>The story concerns a group of 23 people marching across their world against a wind that is always changing but never stops. They are the 34th such "horde" which has been trained since birth to undertake</span>
  <span id="freeText3660976205389201754" style="display:none">I made it to the end! I can hardly believe it! <br /><br />This was a very difficult book to get through. 700 pages of dense, unusual text full of stylistic invention and word-play, with constantly changing narrators, set in a world unlike any I've ever encountered. And in, what is for me, a foreign language.<br /><br />The story concerns a group of 23 people marching across their world against a wind that is always changing but never stops. They are the 34th such "horde" which has been trained since birth to undertake this quest to march all the way to the source of the wind.<br /><br />Even from the beginning, there are hints that this quest is misguided. For example, in the first chapter they pass a city. If there is a city further upwind from where the groups start, then why, after hundreds of years of these hordes, haven't they moved the starting point further upwind? Other revelations in further chapters raise more such issues. The characters themselves aren't immune from wondering, and this becomes one of the major themes of the book: what gives meaning to your quest? or to your life? How do you continue fighting in the face of enormous obstacles when you're not even sure that what you're fighting for makes sense. The characters are all very different and thus find different reasons for continuing.<br /><br />The wind in this place is more than just a normal wind. It is capable of creating some sorts of localized cyclones with basically magical properties. For that reason, I'd call this a work of fantasy. But the wind also has symbolic, metaphoric functions in the story, representing life, energy, speech, and words. Sometimes it is hard to tell where the metaphors end and the literal description begins. (Do the cyclones really display written characters on their sides?)<br /><br />Like any good story, the author is able to make you feel like you are there with the characters, experiencing what they are experiencing and feeling what they are feeling. Unfortunately, what they are mostly feeling is exhaustion and a strong desire to give up. So I felt, at many points, exhausted and wanted to give up. And yet, there was always something there making me want to go just a bit further, and when I did there was always something interesting around the next corner. It almost never went in the direction I expected.<br /><br /><br />The reviews in France are overwhelmingly positive. I'm a bit scared to give anything other than 5 stars, because anyone who does (on some French websites) seems to get attacked and accused of not understanding. I freely admit some (but not all) of the wordplay was over my head. <br /><br />This is a a very original book. That it could be so ambitious and not fail to deliver is very impressive. But based on how much I actually enjoyed reading it and how much I'd like to read more books by this author, or books of this type (if there are any), it is just a bit over 3 stars for me. I'm rounding-up to 4 based on the fact that I greatly enjoyed the wordplay that I understood, especially from the troubadour character Caracole, and the assumption that I would have enjoyed that aspect even more if I spoke French better.<br /><br />Much has been made about the fact that one version of this book was released with an "original soundtrack". Although that is unusual, it isn't the first time such a thing has been done, and I credit that more to the publishing house La Volte than the book author. They have released several such book soundtracks in the past. My favorite being the one for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6718904.Narcose__1CD_audio_" title="Narcose (1CD audio) by Jacques Barbéri" rel="nofollow noopener">Narcose</a> by Jacques Barbéri, on which the author himself performs the music. The soundtrack for "La Horde", which can be heard on the composer Arno Alyvan's website, isn't at all what I would have imagined for this book.<br /><br />I'd be very curious to see a translation. It would be a real challenge to translate. I know it has been translated into Italian, and that an English-language animated movie version, and English-language book is in the works, to be called "Windwalkers". <br /><br />There are so many wonderful, original French SF/F authors, so few of whom have been translated into English. I can only hope that this work can forge a path against the wind for others to follow.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3660976205389201754" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText4934103967648002450" style="display:none">Dear God, this book! It's a shame it hasn't been translated into English (yet!) because I know most of the people reading my goodreads reviews are English speakers. You sould all chain yourself to the front door of your favorite editor to demand a translation (or write an email if you don't feel like chains are the way to go).<br /><br />I loved everything about this novel : the language, the worldbuilding, the characters, the plot, the ideas discussed in between the lines, ... I nearly cried at the end, I was so exhausted by the journey (both the one in the book, and the one that reading itself was). Reading this book was definitely a physical experience, like reading so few books is (Jonathan Strange and Mr Norrell, The Vicomte of Bragelonne when I was 14) : your know, when the story you read is so <i>right</i> that every step a character takes, you take it with him? That book is like this.<br /><br />I'll definitely give it as a present to people I love, so can feel the same joy I did.<br /><br />P.S : English is not my first language, I hope I didn't mangle it too badly.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1557146372" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1557146372" />
    <a title="Ploppy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9950790-ploppy"><img alt="Ploppy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527152864p2/9950790.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1557146372?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ploppy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ploppy" href="/user/show/9950790-ploppy">Ploppy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9950790-ploppy?shelf=france">france</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9950790-ploppy?shelf=21st-century">21st-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9950790-ploppy?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1557146372" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13227484795747949975">After many great and not-so-great reads, there always comes a book which makes you wonder: what the hell have I been wasting my time reading instead of this? And what could I possibly read after finishing it? Since it has just about everything you could ask for (setting, plot, characters, themes, style) why not simply read it again and again?<br/><i>La Horde du Contrevent</i> (literally "The Horde of the Counterwind") is one of those books, shamefully yet untranslated in English. A book that leaves you drai</span>
  <span id="freeText13227484795747949975" style="display:none">After many great and not-so-great reads, there always comes a book which makes you wonder: what the hell have I been wasting my time reading instead of this? And what could I possibly read after finishing it? Since it has just about everything you could ask for (setting, plot, characters, themes, style) why not simply read it again and again?<br /><i>La Horde du Contrevent</i> (literally "The Horde of the Counterwind") is one of those books, shamefully yet untranslated in English. A book that leaves you drained, with that empty feeling you get after becoming so engulfed in the lives of fictional characters, that they had almost become a part of you. Which is one of the great many themes addressed in the book, I might add.<br /><br />On the surface, it is an adventure story, a quest set in an imaginary world where strong winds blow non-stop, making life a constant struggle against the elements. Some people have learned to use the wind to their advantage, building sails and windmills, others cower in fear at each lethal blast which shakes the foundations of their homes. The plot revolves around a group of "horders", an elite band of adventurers who have been chosen to journey all the way to Extreme-Orient, the (imaginary?) place where the wind supposedly originates from. They are the 34th Horde, and their path is built on centuries of knowledge gathered by previous hordes, who each ultimately failed in their quest.<br /><br />This story is told by the various members, there is no omniscient narrator, and each member has his own way of seeing things, and his own specific role. There is Golgoth, the leader/tracker, a strong, brutal figure, whose narrative abounds in strange slang. Sov, the sensitive scribe, who narrates most of the sections, and keeps the horde's "counterjournal", meant to be transmitted to the next horde (at one point he thinks to himself: if we are to believe we're the Last Horde, the ones who will finally accomplish this quest, isn't keeping a journal a sign that we don't really believe it? And how could we accomplish the quest if we don't believe in ourselves?) Oroshi, "windmaster", studies the different types of gusts, and predicts when the next blast will arrive; Caracole, jester, entertains the horde (and the reader) with his stories and unpredictability, and his chapters abound in bouncy rhythms and wordplay. Talweg, "geomaster", studies the terrain, figuring out the best route to take; Erg, the warrior, protects the horde... Then there is Pietro, the prince, who binds the horde together with his sense of duty, his ability to resolve the conflicts that are bound to arise within such a tightly knit group. For <i>La Horde du Contrevent</i> is just as much about the quest pitting the Horde against nature's hostility and their own endurance, as it is about the links that bind the various members together, and the quibbles and clashes that stem from their pride, jealousy, rivalry and more often: from their deciding how to overcome the next possibly fatal obstacle.<br /><br />Alain Damasio makes great use of the polyphonic nature of the narrative, whose shifting points of view enliven the text considerably. The tone itself manages to blend poetic descriptions with coarse dialogue, psychological insight and blockbusting action sequences. He also fits in various areas of knowledge, making use of philosophical concepts, quantum theory and general relativity (without naming them as such) to build a coherent world, fantastical and imaginative on the surface, but whose rules mirror our own at a deeper level. Without going into too much detail, it's as if the various physical forces, which operate on different scales in our world, most of which are invisible to us without the proper instruments, were mixed together and became part of people's daily lives.<br /><br />With all that, it's difficult to pinpoint exactly what <i>La Horde du Contrevent</i> is "about". Whether it's an adventure, a story about love and friendship, about our thirst to discover the unknown forces that govern our universe, or an exploration of philosophical concepts through a fictional narrative (the author is an avid reader of French philosopher Gilles Deleuze, and speaks of his own novels in philosophical terms). In a way, it is the reader's own quest to decide that for himself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13227484795747949975" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1557146372">
  <td colspan="2">
    <div class="updateActionLinks">
        <a class="right flag" rel="nofollow" id="flag_link1557146372" title="Flag this review as inappropriate." href="/flagged/new?resource_id=1557146372&amp;resource_type=Review&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F1397743.La_Horde_du_Contrevent">flag</a>





      <span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_review_1557146372'><a id="like_count_review_1557146372" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/1557146372?resource_type=Review"><span class="likesCount">2 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it gr-button gr-button--small" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F1397743.La_Horde_du_Contrevent">Like</a></span>
&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a href="/review/show/1557146372?book_show_action=true&amp;from_review_page=1">see review</a>
    </div>

<div id="review_3096947248" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3096947248" />
    <a title="Nicolas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/105630228-nicolas"><img alt="Nicolas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586334239p2/105630228.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3096947248?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicolas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicolas" href="/user/show/105630228-nicolas">Nicolas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3096947248" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3345280436213281759">La Horde du Contrevent by Alain Damasio is an experience, more than a book. I chose to give it five stars not for the quality of its prose or the depth of its storyline, but for its uniqueness. The first 100 pages were uneasy and awkward for me, as I could barely understand what was happening. No time is given to the reader to understand the world he is entering. No background information, no map are provided. At the start of the first page, we discover that our heroes (still unknown to us) are </span>
  <span id="freeText3345280436213281759" style="display:none">La Horde du Contrevent by Alain Damasio is an experience, more than a book. I chose to give it five stars not for the quality of its prose or the depth of its storyline, but for its uniqueness. The first 100 pages were uneasy and awkward for me, as I could barely understand what was happening. No time is given to the reader to understand the world he is entering. No background information, no map are provided. At the start of the first page, we discover that our heroes (still unknown to us) are trapped in a storm of wind against which they have to struggle, walk, and hide. The wind is an enemy, but also an object of study for this group of adventurers. They form a team where everyone has a role, and whose leader, the brutal and fascinating Golgoth, is literally first in line to trace a way.<br /><br />No event or narrative device really marks the start of the story. The reader is simply jumping in the train at a random point of a 30-year or so quest (as we are told). He slowly understands that this group of elite explorers was trained from young age to face the wind and walk "back" to its mythical source. Why? No straight answer will ever be given, including to the characters themselves. Depending on the person, obsession, honor, duty, curiosity, entertainment seem to be the main drivers of their hopeless quest.<br /><br />Interesting point, the narration is delivered first person but shared among the different characters of the horde. At the beginning of each paragraph figures a symbol identifying the person currently speaking, sometimes for a sentence, sometimes for ten pages. We therefore explore the author's creation through the eyes of those men and women, very different from each others in all respects but unified in one mad goal: reaching the end of the world.<br /><br />Funnily, I was fascinated by the absence of relatable traits in the characters, and the lack of perspective on the world that we are quite literally exploring through their eyes (we learn as they learn). Identifying to them and then debating about their actions with our own rational (Game of Thrones like) is... really not the point. If the reader is looking for an alternative fully-functioning universe to reflect on his own, he will be disappointed. La Horde du Contrevent is a tale, more than a novel. It will take you far away from your world, and won't show you the way back. It won't make you feel at home and hopeful, but it will appeal to archetypes of your inner self and reflect on the meaning you chose to give to life. It is often said that the journey is the destination. Rarely this aphorism could be more true than here.<br /><br />Unfortunately, this book has not been translated into English.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3345280436213281759" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2203544172" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2203544172" />
    <a title="Olga" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54612104-olga"><img alt="Olga" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2203544172?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Olga" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Olga" href="/user/show/54612104-olga">Olga</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9782070464234" href="/book/show/25135826-la-horde-du-contrevent">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54612104-olga?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2203544172" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1456809252234801910">This book has been on my 'to read' shelf for a while. I have read and highly enjoyed the comics based on this novel so it was time to face my fears (700 pages) and tackle it head on. <br/><br/>It is the journey of 23 people that counter together to reach the source of the wind. These 23 people form the '34th Horde' and they hope to get where no other Horde before them did - 'The Downstream'. Each Horde starts with its members fresh out of infancy at 'The Upstream' and they are bound by strict rules and or</span>
  <span id="freeText1456809252234801910" style="display:none">This book has been on my 'to read' shelf for a while. I have read and highly enjoyed the comics based on this novel so it was time to face my fears (700 pages) and tackle it head on. <br /><br />It is the journey of 23 people that counter together to reach the source of the wind. These 23 people form the '34th Horde' and they hope to get where no other Horde before them did - 'The Downstream'. Each Horde starts with its members fresh out of infancy at 'The Upstream' and they are bound by strict rules and orders guiding their voyage. <br />The wind is the source of their journey and its purpose as they face and try to find all the forms of wind. <br /><br />The story is linear and straightforward. There is no loitering, no small talk and no detour from the straight path. However, the harsh conditions, the mysterious and fantastical elements and the unknown sources trying to halt the Horde at every chance do not make the journey an easy feat. <br /><br />The book is written from the point of view of the 'horde members'. Each paragraph is preceded by a symbol - each horde member has a distinct symbol (the bookmark accompanying the book has all the symbols listed). It is difficult to follow at first, because point of views change frequently and some paragraphs are quite short. Nonetheless, after about a third of the book, it became easier to follow. <br />Some horde members are more present than others, namely the Scribe (Sov), The Prince (Pietro) and the Airmaster (Oroshi). It is difficult to say that each member has a distinct voice of their own. Apart from 2 characters which have defining traits and phrasing that set them apart from the others, the other paragraphs could be attributed to any other horde member. <br />In spite of the length of the book and the excruciating journey , the members don't undergo a lot of character development. The relationships are not delved into and characters don't speak up their thoughts and feelings. Each character has, for the most part, a defining trait and a role to stick to. Fail to stick to the role and you're out of the Horde. <br />This makes it particularly difficult to get attached to any of the characters and their inevitable demise. <br /><br />The ending was... predictable. Along the way, I was hoping that the author surprises with a different ending, taking into consideration the numerous fantastical elements (named 'chrones' in the novel). It was not the case, and the ending makes you desire for more. <br />On the disappointing side as well, the small number of female members and their poor characterization. They often serve only the purpose of men and are seldom referred to as strumpets.<br /> <br />The book hasn't been translated in many other languages. That doesn't surprise me in the least. As a non native french speaker, the Larousse needs to be on hand. The phrasing is sometimes long and difficult and the choice of words make it for quite a poetic read. There is even a whole chapter of word phrasing and word gimmicks.<br /><br />All in all, a highly original science-fiction novel, great world-building and challenging writing style - 3.5 stars. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1456809252234801910" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3186593305" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3186593305" />
    <a title="Tomq" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23195330-tomq"><img alt="Tomq" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3186593305?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tomq" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tomq" href="/user/show/23195330-tomq">Tomq</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3186593305" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4016560083183288396">(I read it in the original French, and it hasn't been translated in English yet. Nevertheless I'm using English here - in case a translation does happen.)<br/><br/>La Horde du Contrevent is seen by many in France as a masterpiece of sci-fi/fantasy. In the years since its publication, it has become a cult classic, been adapted as a bande dessinée, etc. <br/><br/>On the world of the Horde, a powerful wind blows, always in the same direction. This novel tells the story of the thirty-fourth "Horde", a group tasked with</span>
  <span id="freeText4016560083183288396" style="display:none">(I read it in the original French, and it hasn't been translated in English yet. Nevertheless I'm using English here - in case a translation does happen.)<br /><br />La Horde du Contrevent is seen by many in France as a masterpiece of sci-fi/fantasy. In the years since its publication, it has become a cult classic, been adapted as a bande dessinée, etc. <br /><br />On the world of the Horde, a powerful wind blows, always in the same direction. This novel tells the story of the thirty-fourth "Horde", a group tasked with a seemingly simple but inhumanly difficult mission: walking against the wind, all the way, to figure out what is at its origin. The group consists of specialists (a leader, some hunters, a doctor, a scribe, a warrior...) and others who joined them (a bard, load-bearers,...). There's men and women, scholars and murderers. They adopt various formations to force their way through the ever changing wind, and the other lethal dangers thrown at them. Some of these dangers are magical in nature, or at least left without any explanation that could pass as scientific. <br /><br />When we meet the Horde, they're in their early forties, having countered the wind for about three decades. Their quest is, obviously, an allegory for life. Without spoiling the ending, I can write here that the last few pages are both somewhat frustrating and ultimately logical, both for the story and for the allegory.<br /><br />Most people ought to find the allegory interesting, even if they disagree with it. And the plot contains a good amount of tension and suspense, of violence and drama, so this 700-pages book is entertaining, and can be read rather quickly. (Though those who are upset by violence, including from sexist characters, will not enjoy all of this "entertainment". ) <br /><br />So there's a lot of good stuff in this book. But there are also some glaring weaknesses. To name a few:<br />* there's a fine line between allegory and caricature, especially when it comes to characters. Many of the characters are caricatures, including some important ones. <br />* it's very overwritten. You can see the writer, between the lines, trying to look clever at the expense of the story he's telling. He often succeeds, he sometimes fails. Lots of useless gimmicks. <br />* The book contains overtly sexist characters, who are never challenged by others. I don't mind that. Its world has strong gender roles. Fine. But add the way the female characters end up, all of them, and it is hard not to conclude that the author is displaying a sexist bias of his own. <br />* Too many plot holes/dei ex machina, and plot threads left hanging at the end. <br /><br />All in all, it's a nice read... But a masterpiece? I do not think so.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4016560083183288396" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2426009272" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2426009272" />
    <a title="Hotaru" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63821805-hotaru"><img alt="Hotaru" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2426009272?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hotaru" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hotaru" href="/user/show/63821805-hotaru">Hotaru</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63821805-hotaru?shelf=french-lit">french-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2426009272" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17379133316412339081">4.5 stars. If you can read this beautiful oddity in French, do it !! <br/><br/>To get it out of the way, I have to mention that I was somewhat annoyed by some loose ends not tying up and the under-explanation of a number of the MANY concepts thrown at the reader (as well as the fact that the author is, to put it lightly, not much of a feminist). <br/><br/>BUT. BUT. BUT. Imagine a world where the only habiteable place is a (planet-length ?) corridor forged by a mighty stream of wind with many different forms and pow</span>
  <span id="freeText17379133316412339081" style="display:none">4.5 stars. If you can read this beautiful oddity in French, do it !! <br /><br />To get it out of the way, I have to mention that I was somewhat annoyed by some loose ends not tying up and the under-explanation of a number of the MANY concepts thrown at the reader (as well as the fact that the author is, to put it lightly, not much of a feminist). <br /><br />BUT. BUT. BUT. Imagine a world where the only habiteable place is a (planet-length ?) corridor forged by a mighty stream of wind with many different forms and powers, coming from the "Upstream" all the way to the "Downstream", which where most people live (the further away from the source the better). Imagine an entire civilization, its way of life, its tools, its beliefs and cosmogony and its language shaped by the wind. And imagine the fate of a "Horde", with 23 individuals selected and trained from early childhood to accomplish a task specific to them in order, together, to reach the greatest goals of all : walk upwind all the way to the upstream during tens of years to understand the wind and discover its origins. What's at the end? God? An earthly paradise? A scientific explanation for everything? The end of the world? Nothing at all? And who will survive to know? <br /><br />This all makes for a truly unique and gripping book. You get attached to the many characters as each get a turn to describe the Horde's progress upstream. It is a thick book but once I got started I couldn't put it down. Highly recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17379133316412339081" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4700358564977431835" style="display:none">A little gem of a book ! <br />I'm not a big reader nor fan of science fiction but thisis really a must-read for everyone. It's so creative, so well-written. It's not just an amazing science fiction book, it's also a great metaphor on life when you think about it.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>"Live every moment like it's your last, live every moment like it's your first"</b>
</i><br /><br />The more you read this book, the more you get into the story, and the more you start to understand this peculiar world. The author won't hold your attention with long boring description, no, there's just the strict minimum and leaves a lot of freedom to the reader to imagine the world and characters by himself. Instead, there isn't one flat moment in this book, the tension is well-controlled till the end. This keeps you asking for more, everything flows so nicelly, till you finally get to the end, and it's a hell of a satisfaction!</span>

<div id="review_1209123886" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1209123886" />
    <a title="David Wei" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20417707-david-wei"><img alt="David Wei" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368727451p2/20417707.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1209123886?book_show_action=true">Feb 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Wei" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Wei" href="/user/show/20417707-david-wei">David Wei</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1209123886" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10434738326582204328">"DONNEZ-MOI DE LA TERRE... DONNEZ-MOI DE LA TERRE A CONTRER!"<br/><br/>==== Prologue - How I came to read the book<br/><br/>Despite being French, I didn't get to read a lot of French books in my life except for what are considered French classics (Alexandre Dumas, Jules Vernes, Voltaire) or translations of foreign books. I guess it's because most authors I follow regularly are English-speakers.<br/><br/>This lead me to say to a coworker, during a conversation (in French of course) "I read mostly in English because I have the</span>
  <span id="freeText10434738326582204328" style="display:none">"DONNEZ-MOI DE LA TERRE... DONNEZ-MOI DE LA TERRE A CONTRER!"<br /><br />==== Prologue - How I came to read the book<br /><br />Despite being French, I didn't get to read a lot of French books in my life except for what are considered French classics (Alexandre Dumas, Jules Vernes, Voltaire) or translations of foreign books. I guess it's because most authors I follow regularly are English-speakers.<br /><br />This lead me to say to a coworker, during a conversation (in French of course) "I read mostly in English because I have the chance to be able to understand this language quite well and I don't know a lot of French authors that make me want to read them". To what he replied : "Have you ever read 'la horde du contrevent' by Alain Damasio?".<br />He then proceded in describing me how it was an amazing book and a quick summary of the plotline.<br />Another coworker (we're in a small office) heard a bit of the convo and joined in : "Are you talking about 'la horde du contrevent'? Yes, I confirm, it's a great book."<br /><br />Needless to say, it was more than enough to convince me to try it out and here I am.<br /><br />==== My thoughts<br /><br />More than 600 pages later, I feel like I just got back from a farway land. A faraway land where the wind never ceases to blow and can destroy entire villages.<br />'La horde du contrevent' is an amazing journey, a powerful ride, a captivating tale. <br /><br />I haven't read a book so captivating since a long time. I was litterally reading it every night before going to bed until my eyes were sore. Now that I've finished it, I can finally catch up on all the sleeping time I've missed.<br /><br />The story throws right into the midst of it and distills more information as you get along through characters' memories or their new discoveries. <br />Alain Damasio succeeded in creating a whole new world unlike any we've experienced before and likeable / despiseable characters that you would love to have by your side (or not?).<br /><br />Special mention to Caracole who entered the pantheon of my favorite fictional characters.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10434738326582204328" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('h+uq2YoNLlpcUoCJjWh24o7mR0GGmnQFT4t/GDd+0yNnw3DT2Y9SOuyMrvqa16vPQItWb0/y3gnKq7Xgt/D11Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('prwV1XXsWe3Jj1PRqmNwuoJbSIf8q5Kqt7EDzt+XeX5GlM/fJm4ljXlRfaK93K2XTDZZqTXDOKYykck2XxlfiA==')})
  }
//]]>

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_52049749'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/52049749-la-panth-re-des-neiges?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">La Panthère des neiges<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/810151.Sylvain_Tesson?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Sylvain Tesson<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.80 avg rating &mdash; 942 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2019\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer17545344199056867178\">En 2018, Sylvain Tesson est invité par le photographe animalier Vincent Munier à observer aux confins du Tibet les derniers spécimens de la panthère des neiges. Ces animaux discrets et très craintifs vivent sur un gigantesque plateau culminant à 5 00<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText17545344199056867178\" style=\"display:none\">En 2018, Sylvain Tesson est invité par le photographe animalier Vincent Munier à observer aux confins du Tibet les derniers spécimens de la panthère des neiges. Ces animaux discrets et très craintifs vivent sur un gigantesque plateau culminant à 5 000 m d\'altitude, le Changtang. Situé au Tibet septentrional et occidental, il s\'étend sur environ 1 600 km, du Ladakh à la province du Qinghai, et il est habité par les nomades Changpas.\nL\'équipe atterrit à Pékin, puis prend la route à bord d\'un 4X4 en direction du Tibet. Au fil des jours le convoi s\'achemine vers des panoramas de plus en plus grandioses et déserts : là où la population recule, la faune avance et se déploie, protégée des effets nocifs de la civilisation.\nSylvain Tesson décrit une sorte de savane africaine qui serait perchée à 4 000 mètres d\'altitude, où l\'on croise des troupeaux d\'antilopes, des chèvres bleues, des hordes de yacks qui traversent de vastes étendues herbeuses où s\'élèvent des dunes.\nL\'équipe s\'enfonce toujours plus loin, se hissant à des hauteurs qui dépassent largement ce que nous connaissons en Europe. À 5 000 m d\'altitude s\'ouvre le domaine de la panthère des neiges. Dans ce sanctuaire naturel totalement inhospitalier pour l\'homme, le félin a trouvé les moyens de sa survie et de sa tranquillité. Les conditions d\'observation deviennent très difficiles, il faut parfois rester immobile pendant trente heures consécutives par -30° C pour apercevoir quelques minutes le passage majestueux de l\'animal...\nSylvain Tesson entrecroise habilement le récit d\'une aventure exceptionnelle aux confins du Tibet avec des réflexions d\'une pertinence remarquable sur les conséquences désastreuses de l\'activité humaine envers le règne animal. À travers l\'exemple de la panthère des neiges, l\'auteur s\'interroge sur la morphologie d\'un monde où toutes les espèces viendraient à se raréfier puis à s\'éteindre. Il nous entraîne dans cette aventure singulière où l\'on s\'intéresse autant à l\'art de l\'affût animalier qu\'à la spiritualité asiatique.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"17545344199056867178\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n      <div class=\'wtrButtonContainer wtrSignedOut\' id=\'16_book_52049749\'>\n<div class=\'wtrUp Davantage encore que leurs aînées des années 1970, les féministes actuelles semblent hantées par cette figure. La sorcière est à la fois la victime absolue, celle pour qui on réclame justice, et la rebelle obstinée, insaisissable. Mais qui étaient au juste celles qui, dans l’Europe de la Renaissance, ont été accusées de sorcellerie ? Quels types de femme ces siècles de terreur ont-ils censurés, éliminés, réprimés ?\nCe livre en explore trois et examine ce qu’il en reste aujourd’hui, dans nos préjugés et nos représentations : la femme indépendante – puisque les veuves et les célibataires furent particulièrement visées ; la femme sans enfant – puisque l’époque des chasses a marqué la fin de la tolérance pour celles qui prétendaient contrôler leur fécondité ; et la femme âgée – devenue, et restée depuis, un objet d’horreur. Enfin, il sera aussi question de la vision du monde que la traque des sorcières a servi à promouvoir, du rapport guerrier qui s’est développé alors tant à l’égard des femmes que de la nature : une       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/660947.Alain_Damasio">About Alain Damasio</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/660947.Alain_Damasio"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1312836719p3/660947.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/660947.Alain_Damasio">Alain Damasio
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13860460291379700398">Alain Damasio, né Alain Raymond le 1er août 1969 à Lyon, est un écrivain français de science-fiction. Il choisit ce patronyme en l'honneur de sa grand-mère Andrée Damasio.<br/><br/>Né d'un père carrossier et d'une mère agrégée d'anglais1, Alain Damasio obtient un bac scientifique. Après une classe préparatoire HEC, il intègre l'ESSEC, qu'il quitte en 1991. Il choisit de s'isoler (d'abord dans le Vercors pui</span>
  <span id="freeText13860460291379700398" style="display:none">Alain Damasio, né Alain Raymond le 1er août 1969 à Lyon, est un écrivain français de science-fiction. Il choisit ce patronyme en l'honneur de sa grand-mère Andrée Damasio.<br /><br />Né d'un père carrossier et d'une mère agrégée d'anglais1, Alain Damasio obtient un bac scientifique. Après une classe préparatoire HEC, il intègre l'ESSEC, qu'il quitte en 1991. Il choisit de s'isoler (d'abord dans le Vercors puis à Nonza, en Corse) pour s'adonner à l'écriture. Son domaine de prédilection est l'anticipation politique. Il marie ce genre à des éléments de science-fiction ou de fantasy.<br /><br />Jeune, il écrit de nombreuses nouvelles. Son premier texte long vendu à plus de 50 000 exemplaires est La Zone du dehors, roman d’anticipation qui s’intéresse aux sociétés de contrôle sous le modèle démocratique (inspiré des travaux de Michel Foucault et Gilles Deleuze).<br /><br />Son second livre est récompensé par le Grand prix de l'Imaginaire 2006 dans la catégorie Roman. Il s'agit de La Horde du Contrevent (roman accompagné d'une bande-son composée par Arno Alyvan), véritable succès public qui s'est vendu à plus de 100 000 exemplaires2, régulièrement cité dans les incontournables de la science-fiction française.<br /><br />En 2008, il pose sa voix sur Bora5, un morceau de musique de Rone. En 2009, il écrit La Rage du sage (essai politique et poétique sur notre époque) pour le single gratuit Memento mori du groupe SLIVER.<br />Alain Damasio scénarise également Windwalkers, un film d'animation tiré de La Horde du Contrevent, avec Jan Kounen à la réalisation et Marc Caro à la direction artistique.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13860460291379700398" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
